# P0 — Build & Security System

> **The foundation before the foundation.** P0 establishes the guardrail system
> every later phase (P1–P11) runs under: the security concept, the full gate
> system, the build-loop, the dual review, and the test methodology. It is built
> **before** P1 writes any app code, so P1's very first commit already runs through
> the loop + the gates.
>
> Derives from [security-concept.md](../security/security-concept.md) +
> [build-gates.md](../security/build-gates.md). Index: [plan/README.md](README.md).
> Box format: [`_format.md`](_format.md) (the contract `plan-lint` enforces).
>
> **P0 is bootstrapped MANUALLY** (Co-Pilot session + owner — DECISION B,
> [CLAUDE.md](../../CLAUDE.md) §2), **not** by the Build-Loop: P0 *creates* the loop,
> the gate system and the dual review every later phase runs under, so the loop's
> `P1`..`P11` scan deliberately excludes `P0.x` ([`_format.md`](_format.md) §6 step 1).
> The dual review (G1) still applies to each P0 box, driven by hand. The boxes below
> are therefore ordered so the manual build can proceed strictly top to bottom: the
> docs (P0.1) come first because every gate cites them, then the two enforcement
> planes (P0.2), then the gates that need no app code (P0.3), then the language-gate
> *contracts* (P0.4 — buildable now, `→ activated in P1` against real code), the test
> methodology (P0.5), the review/commit protocol (P0.6), and the release-plane gate
> *policy* (P0.7 — built in P10).
>
> **Activation convention** (the content-independence rule above, made concrete for
> this file): a P0 box that authors a gate/contract whose *enforcement target*
> (Rust/TS source, `tauri.conf.json`, coverage data, a built artifact, a staged
> engine) does not exist until a later phase is **fully buildable now** and carries a
> `> → activated in P<n>` note — it is **not** a `needs:` on an unbuilt later box. A
> `needs:` annotation is used **only** for a genuine intra-P0 prerequisite (one P0.x
> box that must be `[x]` before another). This keeps the P0/P1 boundary exact (P0
> authors the contract + wiring-point; P1 wires it against the code it scaffolds) and
> keeps every `needs:` target resolvable on a clean checkout (`plan-lint`
> needs-targets-exist, [`_format.md`](_format.md) §7).

## Boundaries (decided, see plan/README.md)

- **P0 ↔ P1:** P0 builds the gate *system* + content-independent gates + the
  framework/wiring-points for language gates; **P1** wires the language-specific
  gates (clippy/tsc/cargo-deny/…) into the P0 framework as it scaffolds, and
  authors the general governance docs.
- **P0 ↔ P10:** P0 *defines* the release-/supply-chain-gate policy; **P10** builds
  the release pipeline. No double-build.
- **Content-independence rule:** a P0 box may only build what can exist without app
  code. Gates that need Rust/TS to act on are *defined + wired-pointed* here and
  *activated* by the producing phase (annotate `→ activated in P1`).

---

## P0.1 — Security concept & process docs

**Goal:** the living docs that govern how we build exist and are internally
consistent. These come **first** because every gate box below cites one of them and
the doc-consistency gate (G7/G20) cannot pass until they parse.

- [x] **P0.1.1** [DOC] Finalize the security concept — threat→control→gate map complete · §0.11 · G7
  > the security-concept.md §5 table maps all **18** §0.11 classes (T1–T13 incl. T2a/T2b/T2c/T3a/T9a/T9b, the r3 T11 macOS-engine-as-first-TCC-accessor, the r15 T12 unsigned-distribution/download-MITM, and the P2.51 T13 macOS cross-user single-instance socket) to a control + a concrete `Gnn`; enforced by plan-lint check 8. Verifies internal consistency, not new authorship.
- [x] **P0.1.2** [DOC] Finalize the gate catalogue `Gnn` rows + the pin-and-verify policy · G7
  > every `Gnn` cited in a later P0 box's **header `· <Gnn>` refs** exists as a `| **Gnn** |` catalogue row (the `plan-lint` reference-resolution invariant, [`_format.md`](_format.md) §3.1/§7); a **reserved** id (G65/G66/G67) — which by the catalogue's own rule is "a `| **Gnn** |` row only when its control is adopted" and is NOT one today — is therefore named **only in a box's prose `>`-note**, never in a header ref (P0.2.11/P0.7.8/P0.7.15 adopt G67/G66/G65 that way); the gate-ID space is gap-free-or-annotated (plan-lint check 22) and the §0 pin-and-verify / fail-closed / structural-parsing policy is stated. Verifies the catalogue [build-gates.md](../security/build-gates.md) is the authoritative superset (plan-lint check 5).
- [x] **P0.1.3** [DOC] Author the build-loop master prompt — single-branch, 2-session, no fix-push cycle · G1 G7
  > `docs/process/build-loop.md` — the §0 P1..P11 range (DECISION B), §3 selection algorithm, the no-push-between-fix-and-re-review rule. It is the canonical home of the 8-point DoD, the hard-stop numbers, the reviewer rubric and the recorded reviewer-family decision (all authored in P0.6); this box stands the document up so P0.6 fills it.
- [x] **P0.1.4** [DOC] Author the test-strategy doctrine · §6.4 §6.5 · G7
  > `docs/process/test-strategy.md` — the test-levels doctrine, corpus/fixture conventions and the cross-cutting test invariants P0.5 fills in detail. Stood up here so P0.5's boxes have a home.
- [x] **P0.1.5** [DOC] Author roles & escalation — Build-Loop ↔ Co-Pilot ↔ owner · G7
  > `docs/process/roles-and-escalation.md` — who follows a `needs:` (DECISION C, not escalation) vs who escalates a block; the escalation triggers P0.6 references.
- [x] **P0.1.6** [DOC] Author the box-format spec `_format.md` · G7
  > `docs/plan/_format.md` — the four markers `[ ]/[x]/[!]/[!extern]`, the tag taxonomy, sub-boxes, the `needs:`/`unlocked-by:` dependency vocabulary (DECISION C), and the per-phase-file + index convention. This is the contract `plan-lint` (P0.3) enforces, so it precedes the linter; a format change is authored here in the same commit as the `plan-lint` code.
- [x] **P0.1.7** [DOC] Documentation-wiring & context-routing audit + wire the doc-graph gate · §0.11 · G68 G7
  needs: P0.1.1, P0.1.2, P0.1.3, P0.1.4, P0.1.5, P0.1.6
  > the **one-time audit** that the doc/context system is internally honest now that the P0.1 docs exist, plus the wiring point for the G68 doc-graph gate (built in P0.3) — three legs: **(1) DOC-GRAPH** — every `.md` in the canonical **repo-scoped** graph (the seven P0 docs + the spec + the plan + `CLAUDE.md`/SSOT) resolves + is reachable/linked from its proper index (no orphan, no stale/contradictory cross-reference) — the same general "no source-of-truth drifts from the doc graph" property G68 then enforces continuously (this box does the FIRST pass + names the gate's repo-scoped target). **The out-of-repo persistent-memory channel** (the `~/.claude` `MEMORY.md` index + the memory files) is audited HERE, **manually, this one time**, against a concrete **P0→P1 handoff checklist** (at P1-start MEMORY.md MUST carry: (i) the reviewer-family decision + spot-audit cadence, P0.6.3; (ii) the L(-1) change-control policy decision D1 + its `scripts/l-neg1-files.toml` pointer; (iii) a pointer to the gate-status ledger `docs/process/gate-status.md` + the P0-completion record, P0.6.10; (iv) the context-routing principle — loop = lean / Co-Pilot = full; (v) nothing redundant / no stale entry) — the Co-Pilot verifies the checklist is complete BEFORE the autonomous loop starts at P1; explicitly **NOT** a G68 continuous node (it lives outside `git ls-files`, so a repo-scoped gate cannot reach it; this human check is its only audit, build-gates.md §6 check 25 scope note). **(2) CONTEXT-ROUTING assertion** — the [build-loop.md](../process/build-loop.md) §2 read-list POINTS to [security-concept.md](../security/security-concept.md)/[build-gates.md](../security/build-gates.md) for a red-CI lookup but does NOT INLINE the whole gate/security corpus into the lean loop session (no context ballast), while [roles-and-escalation.md](../process/roles-and-escalation.md) / the Co-Pilot carry the full picture — assert the loop = lean (references-not-inlines), the Co-Pilot = full, so a fill-pass cannot quietly paste the corpus into the loop prompt. **(3) WIRE** the G68 doc-graph integrity & freshness gate (P0.3.12) into both planes (its target — the doc graph — exists now, so it is fail-closed from P0, distinct from the structural-map gate whose CLAUDE.md target lands at P1-end). `needs:` every P0.1 doc box because the audit asserts over the full P0.1 set (a natural serialization point — all six P0.1 docs must land before P0.1.7's first-pass audit and the G68 wiring run; see P0.3.12's note).

**Home:** docs/security/, docs/process/, docs/plan/.

## P0.2 — Gate orchestration framework

**Goal:** the two enforcement planes (local git-hooks L1–L3, CI L4/L5) exist as
empty-but-wired harnesses that the P0.3/P0.4 gates plug into. The gate-tool *pinning
mechanism* (P0.2.1) comes first because every other tool here is installed through it.

- [x] **P0.2.1** [GATE,CI] Build the pinned-gate-tool fetch-and-verify mechanism + its wrong-checksum self-test · §3.8 · G24
  needs: P0.1.2
  > the §0 pin-and-verify control: a `scripts/install-gate-tools` that downloads each tool at its committed exact version, verifies checksum/image-digest, and ships a **G24 negative self-test — a deliberately-wrong checksum MUST fail the install**. Pin store covers `lefthook`/`gitleaks`/`actionlint`/`zizmor`/`typos`/`editorconfig-checker`/Semgrep/Syft/`cargo-deny`/`cargo-vet`/`cargo-fuzz`/`minisign`/… A committed **gate-tool source allow-list** (per-tool upstream origin) + each checksum corroborated at pin-establishment against the tool's OWN published signature OR ≥2 independent origins (the G37 acquisition-mode discipline applied to gate tools, which both read CI secrets and catch real findings); a checksum edit is a hard Co-Pilot escalation. `pip`-installed tools use `pip install --require-hashes -r requirements-ci.txt` with a planted-positive that a hashless install fails. Commit `rust-toolchain.toml` (exact stable + date-pinned `nightly-YYYY-MM-DD` for G48), asserted not-floating.
- [x] **P0.2.2** [GATE] Set up the `lefthook` git-hook manager — the L1/L2/L3 plane executor · G54 G24
  needs: P0.2.1
  > install `lefthook` (itself a pinned+checksum-verified tool via P0.2.1 — a poisoned `lefthook` can silently no-op every local hook, the `core.hooksPath`-bypass equivalent, so it carries its own G24 wrong-checksum negative self-test). Author `lefthook.yml` with `parallel` + the perf budgets (L1 soft <10 s, L2 <3 min) and the **chronological plane↔hook mapping: pre-commit = L1, commit-msg = L3 (fires at `git commit`, BEFORE pre-push), pre-push = L2 (fires at `git push`)** — stated so commit-msg is not wired into pre-push or omitted. Empty gate slots that P0.3/P0.4 fill.
- [x] **P0.2.3** [GATE] Build the gate-plane integrity assertion — hooks-installed + not-redirected + two-plane parity + push-from-stale-base · G54 G24
  needs: P0.2.2
  > the after-clone bootstrap is **`scripts/setup-dev`** (`install-gate-tools` + `lefthook install` + a quote-repair of lefthook's unquoted embedded-path so the generated hooks parse on **any** repo path incl. spaces/parens — a lefthook generation bug; a no-op on clean paths; **+ a Windows-only `gpg.ssh.program` pin to the native OpenSSH `ssh-keygen` so non-interactive commit-signing reaches the agent's named pipe instead of hanging on Git-for-Windows' bundled MSYS2 `ssh-keygen` — a P1 addition**); `lefthook install` is mandatory after clone (no local protection without it); G54 resolves the **EFFECTIVE** hooks dir (`core.hooksPath` when set, else `git rev-parse --git-path hooks`) and asserts it holds lefthook-managed hooks, so a `core.hooksPath` redirect to a non-lefthook dir is caught (a redirect silently disables ALL local hooks without `--no-verify`); the two-plane parity (CI re-invokes the same hooks); and the push-from-stale-base guard `git merge-base HEAD origin/main == origin/main`. G24 positive+negative self-test.
- [x] **P0.2.4** [CI] Stand up the GitHub Actions CI skeleton (L4) — clean-checkout matrix · §6.7.1 · G25
  > the L4 clean-checkout job matrix (Win/macOS/Linux) that mirrors L1–L2 (G25) + holds the empty heavy-gate slots P0.3/P0.4 fill. Top-level `permissions: contents: read`; per-job `timeout-minutes`; per-PUSH-workflow `concurrency: {group, cancel-in-progress: true}` (never on the release/tag workflow).
- [x] **P0.2.5** [CI] Stand up the release-workflow skeleton (L5) — tag-triggered, empty gate slots · §6.7.2 · G58
  needs: P0.2.1
  > the `v*`-tag-triggered Lane-B skeleton with empty L5 acceptance-gate slots (P0.7 policy → P10 fill). No secret read in the skeleton; the secret-bearing job is host-bound + token-scoped in P0.2.7/P0.2.10. `needs:` P0.2.1 — like every CI workflow it installs its gate tooling through the pinned fetch-and-verify mechanism (the cluster goal: "the gate-tool pinning mechanism (P0.2.1) comes first because every other tool here is installed through it"), so the dependency is explicit and `plan-lint`-detectable rather than left to document order.
- [x] **P0.2.6** [CI] Wire the CI supply-chain hardening — token scope, SHA-pinned actions, `dependabot.yml`, concurrency · §6.7.2 · G49 G50 G56
  needs: P0.2.4
  > every workflow declares top-level `permissions: contents: read`, elevated per-job only where needed; every third-party action pinned by **full 40-char commit SHA** (not a tag); a `dependabot.yml` covering **github-actions + cargo + npm + pip** (presence asserted by G56); per-PUSH-workflow `concurrency: {group, cancel-in-progress: true}` (never on the release/tag workflow) + per-job `timeout-minutes`. **`id-token` scope sub-rule:** workflow-level `permissions:` sets `id-token` absent/`none`, `id-token: write` ONLY on the release/attestation job (zizmor's excessive-permissions check targets `GITHUB_TOKEN`, not id-token). **`pull_request_target` safe-handler sub-rule:** no such workflow without an Environment-protection gate OR a handler that never checks out / runs fork `head_ref` code. **Cache-hygiene sub-rule:** the secret-bearing job restores no writable shared cache, fork-PR workflows share no cache-key namespace with release/`main`, the signed artifact builds `--locked`/`--frozen-lockfile` cache-cold-or-verified. **Secret-in-log sub-rule:** jq/yq-parsed assertion that the secret-bearing job has no `set -x`, echoes no secret-named env var, `::add-mask::`-wraps secret-derived values + a release-tier post-run log scan for the G2 secret SHAPES. **Delivered in this box (P0.2.6):** the workflow-FILE hardening — top-level read-only perms, full-SHA-pinned actions, concurrency polarity (push cancels / release must NOT), per-job `timeout-minutes`, id-token discipline — enforced by **zizmor** (G50) + **actionlint** (G49) + the stdlib **`check-ci-supply-chain`** (the G56 residual zizmor/actionlint do not cover: dependabot 4-ecosystem presence, id-token, concurrency polarity, timeouts, top-level read-only). **`check-ci-supply-chain` is authored as an _aggressively fail-closed_ stdlib mini-parser** — since a line-scan cannot match a real YAML parser against an adversary, it REJECTS any construct it cannot statically resolve (flow-mapping values at security keys; YAML anchors/aliases/merge-keys/explicit-tags incl. key-level tags; duplicate top-level keys; block-scalar/non-inline/flow permission values; block-list-of-mapping triggers; complex keys) while still classifying depth-aware + scheduled triggers, checking per-job (not just top-level) permission write, and failing the release-cancel side closed; its **61-leg G24 self-test** pins every adversarial-dialect bypass class surfaced across a **7-round adversarial dual review** (zizmor stays the PRIMARY G50 YAML-parsing control). Plus **`.github/dependabot.yml`** (github-actions + pip LIVE; cargo + npm declared, their PRs activate when the manifests land in P1.51). **`→ delivered with the signing job`:** the `pull_request_target`, cache-hygiene and secret-in-log sub-rules and the release-job `id-token: write` all assert the **secret-bearing signing job**, which does not exist until **P0.2.7 / P10** — they land there (the same target-exists deferral the language gates use); `check-ci-supply-chain` meanwhile forbids ANY `id-token` until then.
- [x] **P0.2.7** [CI] Wire CI runner-host integrity — ephemeral hosted signing runner, host-disjoint from the corpus/fuzz VPS · §6.7.2 · G56
  needs: P0.2.6
  > the secret-bearing signing/release step is bound to an **ephemeral GitHub-hosted runner**, **never** the shared self-hosted VPS that runs the Lane-B untrusted-corpus/fuzz jobs (§6.1.4/§6.7.2). The workflow lint fails any secret-using job on a self-hosted label, asserts the corpus/fuzz job and the signing job declare disjoint hosts, and asserts the GitHub-hosted signing job uses `step-security/harden-runner` (BLOCK mode) — asserted ONLY on GitHub-hosted jobs (its free tier is hosted-only; the self-hosted VPS's egress enforcement is G42/G42b + the VPS allowlist + an ephemeral low-priv runner). Implements security-concept principle 11; spec §6.7.2 synced in the same change.
  > **Delivered (P0.2.7):** `check_runner_host` — **check (6)** of `scripts/check-ci-supply-chain` (the same G56 gate + CI workflow-security step; reuses its hardened `structural_lines`/`top_key`/`job_bodies` helpers, **no duplication**). A job that reads a `${{ secrets.* }}` value must (a) NOT be on a self-hosted runner and (b) if GitHub-hosted, carry `step-security/harden-runner` with `egress-policy: block`; a secret job whose `runs-on` is not a **literal recognized hosted image** (self-hosted / custom label / matrix / `${{ }}` expression / list) is rejected **fail-closed**. The **disjoint-hosts** assertion reduces to assertion (a): secret jobs are forced GitHub-hosted while the untrusted-corpus/fuzz jobs run on the self-hosted VPS, so the two host sets are disjoint by construction (security-concept principle 11 names the principle; (a)+(b) are the machine-checkable legs). **Fail-open until the P10 signing job exists** (no `secrets.*`-reading job today → nothing to assert), the standard P0 target-absent posture; 7 adversarial G24 self-test legs (`RH1..RH7`) pin every violation + the non-secret/`secrets.txt`-run-string non-triggers. The spec already documents this control (§6.7.2 / §6.1.4 runner-host carve-out + the §6.7 G56 bullet, authored P0 review r2), so it is already in sync.
- [x] **P0.2.8** [CI] Wire the branch-protection / required-status-checks config assertion · §6.7.1 · G56a
  needs: P0.2.6
  > in the single-branch direct-to-`main` model the only thing that turns a red CI run into a real block is GitHub repo config — invisible to the codebase, silently relaxable in the UI. A scheduled + per-push CI step queries the **rulesets** API for `main` (classic branch protection blocks all direct pushes incl. admins, GH006 — incompatible with direct-to-`main`, so the config is two rulesets), failing if the required status checks are not all present-and-required, if the `non_fast_forward`/`deletion` rules are absent or carry **any** bypass, or if a **non-admin/wider** actor can bypass the required-checks rule (the repo-admin bypassing the *checks* rule is the intended trusted-direct-pusher mechanism); **plus** native secret-scanning + push-protection enabled, default workflow permissions read-only, the T2-taint OR-gate (`code-scanning/default-setup` for `javascript-typescript` OR the G29 rule-(i) Semgrep taint ruleset — machine-enforced as an XOR by plan-lint check 21), and `required_signatures` on `main` (the loop signs its own commits with the P0.7-provisioned SSH key). **Fail-soft during the P0 bootstrap box, then hard.** Spec §6.7.1 synced. (Exempt from the plan-lint check-16 fixture requirement — API-introspection gate, owner-verified instead.)
  > **Delivered (P0.2.8):** [`scripts/check-branch-protection`](../../scripts/check-branch-protection) (**G56a**) — the CORE leg queries the GitHub **rulesets** API (`evaluate_rulesets`): the required-checks rule covers the agreed checks (**subset**) with its bypass set the repo-**ADMIN role ONLY** (the trusted direct-pusher), and the `non_fast_forward`+`deletion` rules exist with **NO** bypass — plus sub-checks **(d)** secret-scanning + push-protection, **(e)** default workflow-perms read-only + `can_approve_pull_request_reviews==false`, **(f)** the T2-taint CodeQL-OR-Semgrep gate, **(g)** the `required_signatures` ruleset rule — each a **pure `evaluate_*()`** function (fixture-driven self-test) over the parsed `gh api` JSON. **Posture:** fail-SOFT in P0 (no `--enforce`: every finding warns, exit 0); `--enforce` (wired in P1) makes a violation or an unreadable required endpoint exit 1. Target-absent legs stay skip-with-warning until their target lands ((g) until the P0.7.17 allowed-signers file; (f) until CodeQL/G29). Wired into the ci.yml `workflow-security` job (**per-push**) + a new **weekly `schedule`** (the UI-drift canary), with the G24 self-test [`g24-branch-protection.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-branch-protection.py) (**44 legs** incl. `ruleset_targets_main`, `bypass_is_admin_only`/`bypass_unreadable`, the admin-only / no-bypass / unreadable-bypass evaluator cases, the (f) read-error hard/soft split + a Semgrep decoy). **Token reality:** GitHub exposes no `administration` token scope (actionlint-verified), so the default CI `GITHUB_TOKEN` cannot read the rulesets/repo-config endpoints — the gate runs **fail-soft in CI** on the default token; the **hard-enforce path is a P1 admin-scoped PAT secret + `--enforce`**, and the live read is **owner-verified**. `[[fail_open]]` row in [`gate-planes.toml`](../../scripts/gate-planes.toml) (G54b now sees 5 exceptions).
  > **Live config PROVISIONED this session (owner present):** first set classic branch protection on `main` — but the live push test hit **GH006**: classic required-status-checks block **all** direct pushes incl. admins (the checks can't be green before the push exists), which **contradicts the §2 direct-to-`main` "red `main`, fix immediately" model**. Escalated as a spec-internal contradiction; **owner decided the rulesets-with-bypass-actor resolution**. Now configured as **two GitHub rulesets** on `main`: (1) `main-required-status-checks` (required checks = `gate-tooling (ubuntu-22.04|macos-14|windows-2022)` + `workflow-security`) with the **repo-admin role as bypass actor** (trusted direct-push works, fork-PRs stay gated), (2) `main-protect-history` (`non_fast_forward` + `deletion`, **no bypass**). Plus default workflow-perms → `read`; secret-scanning + push-protection → enabled. The owner-direct-push then succeeded (`Bypassed rule violations… 4 of 4 required status checks`), and G56a v2 verified GREEN against this live ruleset config, both postures. The `enforce_admins` contradiction was resolved in **build-gates.md G56a check (c)** + **security-concept §3** in this commit. **Still owner-blocked (P0.7, need key material):** the `required_signatures` ruleset rule (SSH signing key), the `release` Environment + 3 secrets, the `v*` tag-protection ruleset, the minisign keypair.
  > **Pulled forward (2026-06-20):** the P1 hard-enforce path is now LIVE — G56a runs `--enforce` **fail-CLOSED** in CI on **push + schedule** with the fine-grained **`REPO_ADMIN_READ_TOKEN`** secret (Administration: Read; the read-only scope is sufficient — verified `--enforce` exit 0 against the live config). Fork-PRs stay fail-soft (GitHub withholds secrets from fork runs; a code PR cannot alter the rulesets anyway). The `gate-planes.toml` G56a `[[fail_open]]` row is **narrowed** ("P1 --enforce pending" → "fork-PR only, covered by push + schedule --enforce"); G54b still sees **5** exceptions. Done in this owner-present session (owner created the read-only PAT, the loop wired the rest), pulled forward so P0's enforcement plane stands fully fail-closed and the gates do not have to be re-touched during the product phases.
- [x] **P0.2.9** [CI] Wire the release-tag (`v*`) trust assertion — the workflow half · §6.7.2 · G56b
  needs: P0.2.5
  > the release-workflow skeleton's **first step asserts the tagged commit is an ancestor of `origin/main` AND main's required checks were green for that exact SHA** (`git merge-base --is-ancestor` + `gh api …/commits/<sha>/check-runs`) and aborts **before any secret is read** otherwise; the `v*` tag must be a signed annotated tag and the step runs `git verify-tag` against the committed SSH allowed-signers file (leg 3 — provisioned in P0.7). G56a guards only the `main` branch ref, not `v*`; legs 2/3 here are fail-closed always. (The tag-protection ruleset POLICY half + allowed-signers provisioning are P0.7.)
  > **Delivered (P0.2.9):** `scripts/check-release-tag-trust` — wired as the FIRST step of the [release.yml](../../.github/workflows/release.yml) `guard` job (after `fetch-depth:0` checkout + an explicit `git fetch origin main` so the ancestry check has a merge-base), running BEFORE the fail-closed-until-P10 step and BEFORE any secret. **Leg 1 ANCESTRY** (`git merge-base --is-ancestor <tag-sha> origin/main`) + **leg 2 GREEN-HISTORY** (`gh api --paginate --slurp repos/<repo>/commits/<sha>/check-runs?per_page=100`, pages flattened, every run completed + success/neutral/skipped, ≥1 present) are **fail-closed always**; **leg 3 SIGNED-TAG** (`git -c gpg.ssh.allowedSignersFile=<f> verify-tag`) is **fail-soft** (skip-with-warning) until the allowed-signers file lands in **P0.7.17**, then fail-closed. The `gh` call uses `${{ github.token }}` (NOT a release secret), so the guard job reads no secret (check-6 fail-open by design). A non-`v*` ref is refused (exit 2). G24 self-test [`g24-release-tag-trust.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-release-tag-trust.py) (14 legs: ref-normalization, the leg-2 green-history parse on fixture check-runs JSON — the live `gh` call is release/owner-verified per the G56a/P0.2.8 API-introspection exemption — and real-temp-git-repo leg-1 ancestry + leg-3 fail-soft/fail-closed) wired into the ci.yml workflow-security job. → **executes at release (P10)**; authored + self-tested now.

  needs: P0.2.1
  > the trust boundary is "everything that touches the bytes that get minisigned": digest-pin the CI base image/container; version/digest-pin the C/C++ toolchain + Tauri CLI/bundler; if engines are from-source, the source tarballs are hash-pinned + the build container digest-pinned (§3.8). **`cargo-fuzz` invokes the date-pinned nightly EXPLICITLY** (`cargo +nightly-YYYY-MM-DD fuzz`), never a bare `+nightly` (cargo-fuzz's internal `+nightly` does not necessarily honour `rust-toolchain.toml`'s channel) — asserted by an actionlint/workflow-lint check that the fuzz job names the date-pinned channel.

The **digest-pin POLICY** (CI base image/container, C/C++ toolchain, Tauri CLI/bundler, from-source engine tarballs) is **§3.8** and is *executed per-engine in P4–P7 + the release container in P10* (the standard policy-here/execute-later split); the **Rust toolchain itself is already pinned** by `rust-toolchain.toml` (exact stable `1.96.0`) + the `nightly-YYYY-MM-DD` fuzz pin in gate-tools.toml, both asserted not-floating by P0.2.1.

  needs: P0.2.2
  > the **owner-ack pre-push enforcement of DECISION D1** (security-concept §2, build-gates.md G71): a `git`-based pre-push check over the push range that fails any commit whose diff touches an L(-1) file unless its body carries `^L-neg1-ack: owner$` (the trailer is the only escape — **no** check-off/`[!extern]` exemption for an L(-1) edit; the §2-vs-plan conflict resolves to §2, since an unrestricted exemption would waive the ack on exactly the gate catalogue / hooks / toolchain it guards). Ships the G24 positive+negative self-test (no-trailer ⇒ fail post-P0; well-formed `L-neg1-ack: owner` trailer ⇒ pass; non-L(-1) diff ⇒ pass). The autonomous Build-Loop NEVER edits an L(-1) file (build-loop.md §6, roles-and-escalation §4(g)).

[`scripts/check-l-neg1-ack`](../../scripts/check-l-neg1-ack) (**G71**) — a stdlib `tomllib`+`git` gate: a glob matcher (`**`/`*`/`?`) over the cage and the `^L-neg1-ack: owner$` trailer audit over the range (`@{u}`→`origin/main` chain, or an explicit `--base`). **The trailer is the ONLY escape** — a commit touching no L(-1) file needs none, but there is **no** check-off/`[!extern]` exemption for an L(-1) edit (the §2-vs-plan conflict, resolved to §2 in the G1 review — see below). **Posture:** fail-SOFT in P0 (a missing trailer warns, exit 0); `--enforce` (P1) → exit 1. Wired **L2** (lefthook pre-push) + the **L4 mirror** (ci.yml `workflow-security`, `--base "$BEFORE"` = `github.event.before` via env so no template-injection, `fetch-depth: 0`). G24 self-test [`g24-l-neg1-ack.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-l-neg1-ack.py) (**53 legs**: the glob matcher's caged-positives (incl. `rust-toolchain.toml`) / not-caged-negatives (the plan + SSOT are NOT L(-1)), the ACK-regex units, + a **real temp-git-repo E2E** — no-trailer fails under `--enforce` / fail-soft passes / with-trailer passes / a check-off + a `[!extern]` over an L(-1) file each NEED the ack / a plan-only check-off + a non-L(-1) edit pass / a `rust-toolchain.toml` bump fails). Auto-discovered by the P0.2.13 canary (now **8/8**). **G1 review** (volle Härte) caught **three P1 holes**, all fixed: (1) a **cage GAP** — `rust-toolchain.toml` self-declares L(-1) but no glob matched it (added + synced across §2/cage/G71-row/plan); (2)+(3) the **`[!extern]` + check-off exemptions** blanket-waived the ack on L(-1) files (the gate catalogue, hooks, toolchain) — §2 sanctions ONLY the trailer, so both exemptions were **removed** (a commit touching no L(-1) file still passes; a plan check-off touches only `docs/plan/**`). Verified: 53/53, G71 live 0, actionlint/zizmor/check-ci-supply-chain 0. **This completes the P0.2 cluster.**

**Home:** build-gates.md §0–§4 · 06-build-test-release (record the `actionlint`/`zizmor`/token-scope CI hardening in the spec per the living-doc rule).

## P0.3 — Content-independent gates (buildable now)

**Goal:** every gate that needs no app code is live on both planes (L1/L2 local +
L4 mirror). These are the boxes that protect P1's very first commit. Each is
fully buildable now; a box whose *target* file lands in P1+ (the CSP conf, the
codegen output) is authored here and carries a `> → activated in P<n>` note.

- [x] **P0.3.1** [GATE] Build the secrets / credential scan — `gitleaks` + the minisign-key custom rule, four legs · G2 G24
  needs: P0.2.2, P0.2.4
  > pinned `gitleaks`; committed `.gitleaks.toml` with a **custom rule for the minisign secret-key shape** (the default PEM rule cannot catch a minisign key — no `-----BEGIN-----` envelope) + the fixture-key allowlist + a one-time baseline. **All THREE real CI secrets named, provably caught, planted-positived:** `MINISIGN_SECRET_KEY` (custom rule), `MINISIGN_PASSWORD` (entropy + env-name scan + a banned `MINISIGN_PASSWORD=<value>` literal), `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` (`sk-ant-…`, the reviewer-API secret — gitleaks' bundled Anthropic rule + a planted-positive). **Current subcommands** (v8.19+ deprecated `protect`/`detect`): `gitleaks git --staged` at L1; `gitleaks git @{u}..HEAD` range leg at L2 (the last local catch before a secret goes public — excluded from the docs-only fastpath; the `@{u}`-unset fallback chain `→ origin/<branch> → origin/main → origin/HEAD → HEAD` with a G24 first-push self-test); `gitleaks dir` full-tree at L4; full-**history** `gitleaks git` at the release tier on a nightly `on: schedule:` trigger, its CI job `actions/checkout` with `fetch-depth: 0` (a default shallow checkout silently scans only the tip; a G56/G49 sub-assertion asserts it). Allowlist/baseline growth-lint (box-id + Dual-Review note + content-fingerprint that rotates); `.gitleaks.toml` + baseline join the L(-1) security-critical-file set. CI uses the pinned, vendored, checksum-verified `gitleaks` BINARY (not `gitleaks/gitleaks-action`, which requires a commercial license for org-owned repos).
  > **Delivered (P0.3.1):** **gitleaks v8.30.1** pinned in [`gate-tools.toml`](../../scripts/gate-tools.toml) (per-OS SHA256 verified against the official checksums.txt + a 2nd independent origin — the Scoop bucket records the identical windows SHA; no build-provenance attestation exists for gitleaks, residual noted). [`.gitleaks.toml`](../../.gitleaks.toml) `[extend].useDefault` + **3 custom rules**: **minisign-secret-key** = `\bRW[A-Za-z0-9+/]{180,}={0,2}` — **verified against a real minisign-0.12 key**: both KDF variants (`RWQA…` passwordless, `RWRT…` password) are `RW` + ~212-char base64, and the **length floor excludes the ~56-char public key** (a fixed `RWRTY0Iy` prefix would have MISSED passwordless keys — caught at build time); **minisign-password-literal** (a `MINISIGN_PASSWORD=<value>` literal, excluding the `${{ secrets.* }}`/`$ref` forms by char-class); **anthropic-api-key-custom** (`sk-ant-…`, a distinct id so it stacks with gitleaks' builtin). The driver [`scripts/run-gitleaks`](../../scripts/run-gitleaks) centralises 4 modes — `--staged` (L1), `--range` (L2, the `@{u}`→`origin/main` fallback chain, full-scan on first push, **never docs-only-skipped**), `--dir` (L4 clean-checkout; gitleaks `dir` does NOT scan `.git`, so the committed fixture isn't re-flagged), `--history` (L5, with a **runtime shallow-checkout refusal** — stronger than a static `fetch-depth:0` lint). Wired: lefthook **L1**+**L2**, ci.yml gate-tooling **L4**, the new [`secrets-history.yml`](../../.github/workflows/secrets-history.yml) **nightly L5** (`fetch-depth: 0`). **Growth-guard** [`scripts/check-gitleaks-allowlist`](../../scripts/check-gitleaks-allowlist) guards every way the config could SWALLOW a secret: it freezes the allowlist `paths`, forbids value-level (`regexes`/`stopwords`) blankets, **asserts `[extend].useDefault` stays on** (a `useDefault=false` would silently drop gitleaks' bundled rules), **freezes the custom-rule-id set** (a deleted/renamed named-secret rule is flagged), **forbids per-rule allowlists**, and caps the [`.gitleaks-baseline.json`](../../.gitleaks-baseline.json) (`[]`) — a change is an L(-1) edit (the "content-fingerprint"). Planted-positive self-tests: [`g24-gitleaks.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-gitleaks.py) (6 — both minisign variants + the other 2 caught, look-alikes + the production path-allowlist NOT), [`g24-gitleaks-allowlist.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-gitleaks-allowlist.py) (12 — every growth/blanket/useDefault/rule-deletion/per-rule shape), [`g24-run-gitleaks.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-run-gitleaks.py) (2 — the first-push fallback). Canary now 11/11. Cage: `l-neg1-files.toml` += `scripts/run-*` (run-gitleaks was otherwise uncaged) + `.gitleaks-baseline.json`. The `.env` (gitignored, untracked) is deliberately NOT path-allowlisted (that would hole a force-added `.env`; git-mode catches a committed one; the local-`dir` `.env` finding is a dev artifact — the CI clean checkout has none). **G1 review** (volle Härte) returned GO (no real secret evades, no real one is swallowed without owner-ack); the applied P2/P3 fixes: the anthropic custom rule got a **distinct id** (`anthropic-api-key-custom`) so it STACKS with gitleaks' builtin (no id-collision dedup), the growth-guard gained the **useDefault / rule-id-freeze / per-rule-allowlist** checks above, and the run-gitleaks usage docstring was corrected. **Deferred (P2, non-blocking):** a MINISIGN_PASSWORD in a multiline YAML block scalar is not caught by the same-line literal rule — the password is useless without the SECRET KEY (caught robustly), and the single-line literal + gitleaks' entropy defaults cover the common forms; a block-scalar rule is a follow-up.
- [x] **P0.3.2** [GATE] Build the WebView CSP + capability structural lint · §0.10 §7.8.2 §7.6 · G47 G24
  needs: P0.2.2, P0.2.4
  > `jq`/`serde_json` parse (not regex) of `tauri.conf.json` `app.security.csp` + `src-tauri/capabilities/*.json`, asserting **structural equality per directive against the literal locked §0.10 CSP object** (the permitted non-`'self'` tokens recorded per directive: `connect-src` = `{ipc:, http://ipc.localhost}`, `script-src` = `'self'`, `img-src`/`media-src` no `asset:`, `object-src`/`frame-src`/`frame-ancestors` = `'none'`, …). [`g24-js-supply-chain.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-js-supply-chain.py) = 68 legs; canary 19/19. Wired L1 + L2 + L4. `.npmrc` is L(-1) (added to the security-concept §2 enumeration + the G71 row + the CLAUDE.md §5 set in the SAME commit). The `dangerouslyAllowAllBuilds` YAML detector is **fail-closed** (flags the key whenever present with any value that is NOT an explicit falsy literal — pnpm copies the raw js-yaml value and gates on a bare truthiness check, so `yes`/`on`/`y`/`1`/`"true"`/`!!bool true` all enable it, not just `true`). The TS gate contract that consumes this is P0.4. **G1 review (volle Härte) NOGO → fixed → re-reviewed:** (P0 doc-sync) `.npmrc` was caged in `l-neg1-files.toml` but missing from the §2/G71/CLAUDE.md prose — synced (DoD item 2). (P1 activated-tier hardenings, fixed not deferred) the resolution-URL guard now rejects **non-registry schemes** (`git+`/`git:`/`ssh:`/`file:`/protocol-relative `//` = clone-and-build code-exec), not just foreign `https` hosts; `evaluate_npmrc` now rejects a **scoped `@scope:registry=` override** to a non-allowed origin (source-substitution); the `onlyBuiltDependencies` count is **fail-closed** on a present-but-unparseable allowlist + scans pnpm-11 `allowBuilds` + a comment-in-block list; and a **committed manifest WITHOUT a lockfile FAILS** (mirrors the Rust `check-supply-chain` workspace-state, never a silent skip). **Round 2 (NOGO → fixed) — two further source-substitution vectors the skeptic verified against the pnpm docs:** the gate now scans the pnpm-workspace.yaml **`registries:` block** (the YAML default/per-scope registry-pin analogue — every value must be the allowed origin, fail-closed on an inline/anchor form), and **forbids a committed `.pnpmfile.cjs`/`pnpmfile.cjs`** outright (install-time custom fetcher/resolver code can re-source any dependency while the recorded lockfile URL still reads npmjs.org — no place in a zero-egress product). **Round 3 (NOGO → fixed) — completing the "committed config mutates source / runs install code while the resolution URL stays npmjs.org" class:** the gate now forbids a **non-root `.npmrc`** (pnpm reads per-directory `.npmrc`, so only the single root pin is allowed), forbids **pnpm `patchedDependencies` + a `patches/` dir** (an install-time patch mutates a third-party dep's source, URL-scan-blind), flags **source-redirecting `overrides`/`resolutions`** (`file:`/`link:`/`git`/url targets the URL-scan can't see) **in BOTH `package.json` AND `pnpm-workspace.yaml`** (pnpm 11 reads overrides only from the yaml — the primary location), and forbids **root `package.json` install-lifecycle scripts** (`pre/post/install`/`prepare`/`preprepare`/`postprepare`/`prepublish`/`dependencies`). **Round 4 (NOGO → fixed) — completing the source-redirect class on the DIRECT door:** a `file:`/`link:`/`portal:`/`git+` spec in a direct `dependencies`/`devDependencies`/`optionalDependencies`/`peerDependencies` entry, OR in a pnpm `catalog:`/`catalogs:` version-catalog, is now caught (it escapes the lockfile-URL backstop — a local dep is recorded as `type: directory` with no URL). The full committed-config pnpm dependency-spec + install-code surface is now frozen; a **subdir `package.json`** in a future multi-package workspace is the one recorded P1-activation refinement (v1 is a single front-end package — only the root `package.json` + the workspace yaml exist). **Round 5 (NOGO → fixed) — the registry-sourced install-injection class:** the gate now forbids pnpm **`configDependencies`** (a registry-sourced config package that injects `.pnpmfile.cjs` hooks / patch files / the build allowlist before graph resolution — defeating three forbids at once behind a clean registry tarball) + **`onlyBuiltDependenciesFile`** (a file-pointer that sidesteps the inline allowlist count), and scans **`packageExtensions`** injected sub-maps for source-redirects. **Round 6 (NOGO → fixed) — the last two pnpm-10.13.1 dangerous-class names:** the `.pnpmfile.cjs` forbid is extended to `.pnpmfile.mjs`/`pnpmfile.mjs` (the ESM form is pnpm's *default* `pnpmfile` name), and **`dangerouslyAllowAllBuilds`** (pnpm 10.9.0+, auto-runs every dependency's build script with no allowlist) is forbidden. **Convergence:** the covered surface is the committed-config install/source-substitution surface of the **pinned pnpm 10.13.1** (§0.8) — bounded, not open-ended; a pnpm pin bump is itself an L(-1)/pin-and-verify change that triggers a re-audit of this gate. (Out of scope, affirmed: `namedRegistries` is pnpm 11.1 — pin-bump re-audit; proxy/ca/ignoreScripts/neverBuiltDependencies are not dangerous-class.) (P2 residual, recorded: a `npm:`-alias override + the JS package-NAME typosquat are the reserved-G18e name-trust residual; an `overrides` foreign-URL target is additionally backstopped by the resolution-URL scan once the P1 lockfile lands.)

Per artifact: run the **exact** named regen command → `git diff --exit-code <path>` (regeneration that changes the file = drift = FAIL; a wrong/stale codegen invocation cannot silently pass) → a **structural (parsed, not regex) non-empty** validator (`json` parse+non-empty / `text` non-blank / `ts-bindings` non-blank + has `export`) that catches a truncated emit a pure diff misses when the committed copy is also truncated. Wired L2 + L4 (a push-tier by-glob gate — regen is too slow for the L1 realtime pass). `check-generated-drift` is L(-1). **G1 review GO** (3× GO); the git-tracked structural guard was landed on the reviewers' recommendation. **Recorded P1-activation obligations** (the registry is empty/dormant in P0): the framework cannot verify a black-box regen-argv is the *real* producer (a no-op regen on a stale-but-valid tracked file passes — the P1 registrant must name the genuine producer), and nothing forces `ARTIFACTS` non-empty once `bindings.ts`/the manifest land (a P1 that forgets to register a producer stays silently green) — both are P1-registration items carried here.

The **(e) prose-vs-invocation** subtlety is solved structurally per file type: YAML strips only `#` comments + keeps `run:`/scalars (the realistic auto-refresh vector + the row-mandated self-test fail); Python/TOML/shell blank `#` comments **and** every string literal, so the gate's own pattern definition, its self-test fixtures, and other gates' prose mentions of the rule yield 0 hits when scanned live (a self-test asserts 0 hits over the gate's OWN source **and** the self-test's OWN source) — the residual Python-`os.system`-string vector is covered downstream by **G18a**'s `imports.lock`-in-the-diff check. **(d)** blanks comments but keeps strings (a `"http://localhost"` literal is caught, a `// localhost` comment is not), exempts `#[cfg(test)]` via a string-aware brace match robust to `println!("{}")`, and carves the three pinned `bundle/LibreOffice*` globs (first-party code stays localhost-banned with no exception). **(b)** matches only the qualified `(std|tokio)::process::Command::new` (NOT a bare `Command::new` — a clap builder's form; that is **G29**'s import-resolving job). Carve-out paths for (b)/(c)/(f) [Build-Session-Entscheidung: P0.3.10] are picked robust to the unknown P1 crate layout and confirmed when the real code lands (a carve-out change is itself a reviewed L(-1) edit). [`g24-repo-invariants.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-repo-invariants.py) = 112 legs; canary 21/21. Wired L1 (pre-commit) + L4 (`gate-tooling`). The gate + its self-test are L(-1) (`scripts/check-*` / `scripts/gate-selftests/**`, already caged — no `l-neg1-files.toml` edit needed). **G1 review (volle Härte) — 4 NOGO rounds → GO.** *Round 1:* a **P0** in the LIVE (e) invariant — a real `cargo vet update` SPLIT across physical lines (YAML folded `run: >-` / plain multiline scalar / shell `\`-continuation) folded into the executable command but the per-physical-line scan missed it (G18a backstop target-absent in P0 → no compensating control); + four **P1**s fixed not deferred: (d) `#[cfg(not(test))]` no longer mistaken for a test gate; (d) a non-block `#[cfg(test)]` no longer leaks `pending`; (a)/(c) blank comments + neutralise `href`/`url(#…)` fragment-refs + anchor `Send`/`Sync` to the implemented-trait position (no more `href="#fff"`/PR-ref/`<T: Send>`-bound false-positives); shell = command-lang (string-wrapped `eval` caught); (f) scope broadened to `.test.tsx`/`__tests__/`. *Round 2:* the round-1 (e) fix introduced **two NEW defects**, both fixed — a **P0** re-bypass (a `#` on a continuation line of an open quote truncated a multiline-quoted scalar, dropping a trailing `; cargo vet update`) and a **P1** cross-line false-join (a blanked comment / same-indent sibling bridged `cargo vet` + a later `update`). *Round 3:* the round-2 rewrite introduced two **false-positives** (both fixed): a **P1** word-internal-apostrophe phantom quote that kept a downstream prose comment, and a sibling false-join where indented SHELL lines were folded as if YAML (indent-fold is now YAML-only). *Round 4:* the round-3 apostrophe guard **re-opened a P0 false-negative** — in SHELL a quote opens word-adjacent (`X=a"b # c"` quotes `b # c`, so a trailing `; cargo vet update` EXECUTES) but the "not after a word char" guard suppressed the opener and stripped the real invocation. Fixed by making the opener rule **language-specific**: SHELL `'`/`"` always open (a word-internal `'` in shell is itself an unbalanced-quote syntax error → over-flagging blocks no legit push); YAML opens only at a scalar start (fixes the contraction FP, and a YAML ` #` after a plain scalar is a real comment). Final (e): comment-stripping is **quote-aware across lines** with a **language-specific opener** (shell always opens, YAML only at scalar start), fail-safe on an unbalanced quote; matching is **per logical line** folding only a genuine shell `\`-continuation (odd trailing-backslash count) or — YAML-only — a more-indented scalar body, never an arbitrary newline. P2/P3 (YAML narrow-to-run-keys, literal-`|` over-join, a `\`+trailing-whitespace over-fold, Rust raw/byte-string brace handling, deeper nested generics, `cfg(not(not(test)))` — all fail-safe over-flags) recorded as P1-activation refinements.

A **width-agnostic tree-art parser** `_parse_tree_dirs` reconstructs the repo-relative DIR set from a fenced `├──/│/└──` block via an indent STACK (the parent of a line = the nearest shallower-indented dir) — robust to the §1a (4-col) vs §0.7 (3-col) connector widths, and it additionally mines **same-line sibling dirs** (`a/  b/  c/`) and **embedded-path ancestor dirs** (`lib/ipc/x.ts` ⇒ `lib`, `lib/ipc`). `_fenced_block_after` locates the §1a block (CLAUDE.md `## 1a`) and the §0.7 "Physical tree" block; `_git_tracked_dirs` derives the on-disk dir set from `git ls-files` (tracked only, so untracked scratch never false-fails) minus the committed `_STRUCT_IGNORE` set (`target`/`node_modules`/`dist`/`.git`). `_struct_map_relations` (pure, set-only) asserts the **three** edges: (1) **disk ⊆ map** (a tracked folder with no map row fails), (2) **map ⊆ disk** (a stale map entry fails), (3) **map ⊆ §0.7** (the projection bind — §1a may not invent a dir §0.7 does not home, §0.7 the higher source). **`→ activated in P1`:** SKIPS while the **§1a SECTION** still carries the word `PLACEHOLDER` (a section-scoped, not whole-file, signal — `_section_text`), then fail-closes — a missing/unparseable §1a-map or §0.7 block, or an unavailable `git`, all fail CLOSED once active (never a silent skip). [`g24-plan-lint.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-plan-lint.py) **71 → 93 legs** (+22: parser nested/sibling/embedded/root, the 3 relations, `_dirs_from_files` incl. ignore, the fence-finder both ways, skip real+synthetic, the active path through real `git ls-files` in BOTH directions, the active fail-closed branches, and the G1-hardening regressions). **G1 review (volle Härte):** 3 parallel reviewers (correctness / integration / security-skeptic) + an Opus synthesizer all **GO, no P0/P1** — every parser mis-parse fails in the SAFE false-positive direction; the latent false-negative shapes need an authoring convention the real map does not use, and the gate is dormant until P1.64. **Hardenings applied this commit (per the §6 cleanest-wins rule, beyond the noted-only requirement):** (a) `_name_tokens` now strips the annotation (everything from the first `→`/`#`/`(`) BEFORE tokenizing, so trailing prose can never inject phantom dirs; (b) embedded-path ancestor mining runs ONLY on the tree NODE (token 0) — same-line siblings must be SIMPLE single-segment dirs; (c) `_git_tracked_dirs` uses `git -c core.quotepath=false ls-files -z` (raw UTF-8, NUL-split — no octal-mangled non-ASCII dir names); (d) the skip signal moved from a whole-file `PLACEHOLDER`/`P1.64` scan to **§1a-section-scoped `PLACEHOLDER`**, so a `[P1.64](…)` provenance link can no longer pin the gate permanently dormant after P1.64; the G68 §0.7-fingerprint dormancy was aligned to `["PLACEHOLDER"]` for the same reason; (e) the §0.7 `Physical tree` header regex is heading-anchored. **P1.64 reconciliation obligations surfaced by the gate (recorded):** (1) the current §0.7 enumerates only the CODE subtree and does NOT home `docs/`, `assets/`, `supply-chain/`, `.github/workflows/`, `docs/spec/04-formats/`, nor the `scripts/gate-selftests/*`/`tests/g53-fixture/*` subdirs — so P1.64 MUST first expand §0.7 to the COMPLETE tracked tree (else the projection bind flags §1a's `docs/`), remove the `PLACEHOLDER` stub block so the gate activates, + re-bless the G68 §0.7 fingerprint, all in the same commit; (2) the §1a map AND §0.7 must list every dir as an EXPLICIT row at its natural depth — `_parse_tree_dirs` infers intermediate ancestors from an embedded path, so a map omitting a parent but listing a child would not raise disk-not-in-map for that parent (a P1.64 authoring discipline + a self-test fixture to add then). Wired through the existing plan-lint L1/L2/L4 call sites; the `git ls-files` walk runs only on the active (post-P1.64) path, so the P0 skip path stays dependency-free.
- [x] **P0.3.14** [GATE] Build the test-suppression-marker gate — the "no green-by-rewrite" mechanical signal leg · §6.4.2 · G70 G24
  needs: P0.2.2
  > the **G8-deferral analogue applied to TESTS** (G70), built as a diff-based / `plan-lint`-family scan with the same diff-scoped-at-L1-fail-open-without-base / full-tree-fail-closed-at-L2-and-L4 posture as G8/G21. It scans a diff for an **added test-suppression marker** in a test file (`*.test.ts`/`*.spec.ts` / a `*.rs` test under `tests/` or a `#[cfg(test)]` block) — `#[ignore]`, `#[cfg(ignore)]`, `it.skip`/`describe.skip`/`.only`, `test.skip`, `xfail`, a `#[should_panic]` retro-fitted onto a previously-real assertion, or a REMOVED/commented-out assertion in a changed test — and **FAILS UNLESS a `[Test-Change: <box-id> — old-obsolete+new-correct, §ref]` justification tag sits within ±N lines** (the same ±-line-window suppressor discipline as G8; the net-new form `[Test-Change: <box-id> — new-test:<reason>, §ref]` covers a marker in a brand-new test that has no prior expectation to obsolete). It is the **mechanical SIGNAL leg** of the "no green-by-rewrite" discipline (**doctrine home = [test-strategy.md](../process/test-strategy.md) §8**; the `· §6.4.2 ·` header ref homes it at the in-core test-pipeline anchor as the nearest spec §, since G70 is a `plan-lint`-family meta-gate that diff-scans test files rather than its own spec-§ test level — deliberate, not incidental): the catastrophic failure mode is a model that bluntly rewrites/relaxes a red test until green and HIDES a real regression. **It FLAGS + REQUIRES JUSTIFICATION, it does NOT forbid** — a marker carrying the `[Test-Change]` tag passes normally (changing a test is necessary in the common case and stays a first-class move). The **SEMANTIC** "is this rewrite suppressing a real regression?" call is NOT G70's job — it is the **G1 dual-review test-integrity scrutiny item** (P0.6.1), exactly the G8↔G1 split (G8 flags the deferral marker, G1 judges the design). Ships a **G24 positive+negative self-test** (an `#[ignore]`/`it.skip`/a removed assertion in a changed test WITHOUT a `[Test-Change]` tag MUST fail; the same marker WITH a well-formed `old-obsolete+new-correct` tag MUST pass; a net-new `#[should_panic]` test carrying the `new-test:<reason>` tag MUST pass; a clean test diff MUST pass) registered in `scripts/gate-selftests/` so plan-lint check 16 is satisfiable for G70.
  > → activated in P1 (the gate's scan logic + self-test are authored now; the first real test files it scans land from P1 onward, so it fails-open/skip-with-warning over a test-file-less tree and fail-closes as soon as test files exist — the same bootstrap posture as G22/G23).
  > **Delivered (P0.3.14):** [`scripts/check-test-suppression`](../../scripts/check-test-suppression) — the G8-deferral structure (`--diff` L1 fail-open-without-base / `--full` L2+L4 fail-closed) applied to TESTS. **Scope** (`test_scope_lines`): a `*.test.*`/`*.spec.*` or a `*.rs` under `tests/` is wholly test code; any other `*.rs` contributes ONLY its `#[cfg(test)]` block(s) (a brace-matched range via `_cfg_test_ranges`, string/comment-aware so a `"}"`/`// }` never miscounts — a marker in production code is NOT flagged). **Markers** (CODE tokens, not prose): Rust `#[ignore]`/`#[cfg(ignore)]`/`#[cfg(any())]`/`#[cfg_attr(…, ignore)]`/`#[should_panic]`; TS/JS `it.skip`/`describe.skip`/`test.skip`/`.only`/`.skipIf`/`.runIf`/`xit(`/`xdescribe(`/`fit(`/`fdescribe(`/`it.todo`/`xfail`. **Diff-only signals** (`--diff`, via `_scan_hunks` over `git diff --unified=6`): an ADDED marker, a REMOVED assertion (`-` line matching `assert!`/`assert_eq!`/`prop_assert!`/`assert_matches!`/`ensure!`/`expect(`/a chained `.toBe…` even on its own line), or a newly COMMENTED-OUT assertion. **Suppression:** a `[Test-Change: <box-id> — old-obsolete+new-correct, <ref>]` OR `[Test-Change: <box-id> — new-test:<reason>, <ref>]` tag within ±6 lines — `TAG_RE` requires a real `P<n>…` **box-id** (an un-traceable tag with no box-id, or with neither sanctioned shape, does NOT suppress). It **FLAGS + REQUIRES JUSTIFICATION, does not forbid** — the semantic "is this rewrite swallowing a regression?" call is the G1 dual-review's (the G8↔G1 split). Line-comment-aware (`_line_comment_stripped`, string-aware so a `//` in a URL is not a comment), so a marker MENTIONED in a `//` comment is not flagged. [`g24-test-suppression.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-test-suppression.py) = **43 legs** (rust+ts markers incl. the extended set, the `#[cfg(test)]` scoping both ways, both tag shapes + the ±6-window + a malformed-tag + a no-box-id negative, comment-stripping, the diff signals with/without tag, the multi-line-literal/lifetime scope-escape regressions, a real temp-git-repo `--diff` E2E [no-tag⇒rc1 / tag⇒rc0 / fresh-repo fail-open⇒rc0]); canary 23→24. **Not fully target-absent today:** the 2 committed `tests/g53-fixture/**/src/*.rs` crates ARE in scope (clean — no markers), so `--full` is LIVE now, not skip-with-warning. Wired **L1** (lefthook pre-commit `--diff`) + **L2** (pre-push `--full`) + **L4** (ci.yml `--full`); the gate + self-test are L(-1) via `scripts/check-*` / `scripts/gate-selftests/**` (no `l-neg1-files.toml` edit). **G1 review (volle Härte) NOGO → fixed → re-reviewed:** the **`--full` brace matcher** (the fail-closed plane) miscounted depth on a multi-line `r#"…}…"#` raw string / a backslash-continued string / a lifetime `&'a` eating a `{` — closing the `#[cfg(test)]` scope early so a later real `#[ignore]` escaped; fixed by `_rs_structural`, a stateful pass carrying multi-line string / raw-string / **NEST-aware** block-comment state + lifetime-aware char-literal handling across lines (the G8 `_comment_spans` discipline, extended with Rust block-comment nesting — round-2 review caught that a flat `find("*/")` closed a nested `/* … */ } */` early and ejected a later `#[ignore]`). A **round-3** review caught a further under-flag: a **line-wrapped attribute** (rustfmt emits `#[cfg_attr(\n …,\n ignore\n)]` for a long predicate, and `#[\n ignore\n]` is legal) evaded the per-line marker scan — fixed by `_rs_attr_joined`, which collapses a multi-line `#[ … ]` onto its opening line (bracket-depth-tracked over the structural code) before the marker regexes run, so the wrapped form is caught in the fail-closed `--full` plane. `TAG_RE` gained the box-id requirement (an un-traceable tag no longer suppresses); `ASSERT_RE` gained `prop_assert!`/`assert_matches!`/`ensure!` (this project's first-class property-test assertions) + a chained-`.toBe` on its own line; the marker set gained `#[cfg(any())]`/`#[cfg_attr(…,ignore)]`/`fit`/`fdescribe`/`skipIf`/`runIf`. **Doc-graph cleanup (DoD item 2):** the ci.yml L4-slot comment listed G68/G69 as unfilled slots — they have run inside the `plan-lint` step (checks 25/26) since P0.3.12/13 — and the lefthook.yml gate-slot header still listed plan-lint/G8/G70 as "remaining"; both corrected here. **Recorded residuals (inherited from the G8 model, G1-judged):** the marker set is enumerated-not-exhaustive (behavioural disables like an early `return;`/`if false {}`/`assert!(true)`-weakening are the semantic G1 review's job, not this mechanical signal), and the `[Test-Change]` tag is a textual ±6-line search (a borrowed/in-string tag can suppress an unrelated marker) — identical to G8's `is_suppressed`, accepted for this canary; the `#[cfg_attr(…)]` marker regex's `[^\]]*` stops at a `]` inside a `feature = "x]y"` string (exotic; the identical limitation holds for the single-line form, a `RUST_MARKERS`-regex property — over/under in a non-rustfmt-natural, near-non-compiling input).

**Home:** build-gates.md §2/§4/§6.

## P0.4 — Language & build gate contracts

**Goal:** the contract + CI wiring-points for the language gates are defined; full
activation happens when P1 scaffolds the toolchains.

These boxes author the **contract + CI wiring-point** for each language gate now;
the gate **activates in P1** when the Rust crate / pnpm workspace it acts on is
scaffolded (the P0/P1 boundary — P0 defines, P1 wires against real code). Each
therefore carries a `> → activated in P<n>` note and is fully buildable now.

Fixed: `_attrs_missing` now blanks string/raw-string literals (not just comments) and the deny/allow regexes are **line-anchored to the module-inner `#![…]` form** — which also fixed an over-strict **[P2]** (only a module-wide `#![allow(...)]` disqualifies the deny now; an item-level `#[allow(...)]` — the build-gates G4 `// PANIC:`-justified per-item escape — no longer false-fails); plus a **[P2]** `UnicodeDecodeError` guard on a non-UTF-8 config. **Round 3 (NOGO → fixed):** the skeptic found the round-2 `!`-anchor itself opened two new false-passes — a `#![cfg_attr(all(), allow(...))]` always-on (or `not(test)`/feature-gated) crate-wide relaxation that reads like a deliberate gate, and a same-line `#![deny(...)] #![allow(...)]` the line-anchored allow-regex missed. Fixed: the allow check now splits into a non-line-anchored `#![allow(...)]` matcher (catches the same-line form) + a `#![cfg_attr(<cond>, allow(...))]` matcher (re.S, so a rustfmt-wrapped multi-line cfg_attr is caught) that disqualifies UNLESS `cond` is exactly `test` — so an always-on/production-affecting cfg_attr-allow is caught while the legitimate `#![cfg_attr(test, allow(...))]` test-only escape still passes. Each fix carries its own self-test leg (18→**40** legs). A final convergence-skeptic pass returned **GO**; its one residual (a fmt-violating spaced `clippy :: unwrap_used` allow) was closed too by normalising `::` whitespace in `_attrs_missing`. The static check is now robust to every realistic module-wide relaxation form (direct/string/comment/`panic_fmt`-collision/cfg_attr-non-test/same-line/multi-line/spaced-`::`); the sole remaining residual (a proc-macro-GENERATED attribute) is beyond any static text scan and is backstopped by the P1 G1 dual-review reading the crate root.

The one consolidated **P2** was fixed before push: `decrease_guard` only caught a numeric LOWERING of a SURVIVING key — a floor REMOVED (key in prior, gone in cur) or RETYPED to a non-number was silently dropped from `_floor_map` and escaped (both un-gate the domain). **0 such commands today (only the ci.yml P1 build-step slot comment) ⇒ skip-with-notice, fail-CLOSED the moment a build command lands.** Relies on **G56/G50/G49** to fail-close exotic YAML (anchors/aliases/flow/multi-doc) for the SAME `.github/**` files (so a command cannot be smuggled past the plain-text scan). cargo plugin test-runners (`nextest`/`llvm-cov`) are a documented P1 addition — the box that wires the CI test command verifies their `--locked` against the pinned `--help` then (the G17 r7 discipline), not baked in unverified now. **(C) DRIFT-GUARD (live):** `git diff --exit-code` over the existing `DRIFT_PATHS` (Cargo.lock root-OR-`src-tauri/`, pnpm-lock.yaml, `supply-chain/imports.lock`) — no-op while none exist (the P0 posture), fail-CLOSED the moment one drifts OR git is unavailable/errors (rc∉{0,1} ⇒ "cannot verify", never read as clean). **Distinct from** G18/G18b (the cargo-deny/vet POLICY freeze + ≥2-import-source floor) and G9-(e) (the cargo-vet-mutator command-ban) — G18a catches the missing pin FLAG (B) + the drifted lockfile RESULT (C). [`g24-lockfile-integrity.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-lockfile-integrity.py) = **40 legs** (freeze-gut: drift-set drops, empty pin-set, each forbidden leak, dropped `--locked`, retyped pnpm flag / flag-scan: unpinned+pinned cargo/pnpm, `--frozen`, value-flag-before-subcommand, audit/deny/vet/fuzz/metadata NOT flagged, `pnpm run`/`name:`/sibling-`with:` not scanned, line-continuation, transparent prefix, pipe-split, mixed pinned+unpinned, inline `- run:`, target-absent / drift-guard: no-lockfile no-op, rc=0/1/None/128, path-list); canary 31→32. ---

## P0.5 — Test methodology & harness conventions

**Goal:** *how we write tests* is defined and the cross-cutting test invariants have
a home. Most boxes are doctrine/conventions homed in `test-strategy.md` (P0.1.4); the
cross-cutting security-test *homes* are defined now and `→ activated` by their phase,
so a later phase has a named home rather than re-deciding the methodology.

- [x] **P0.5.1** [DOC] Author the test-levels doctrine — unit/integration/property/fuzz/E2E/a11y · §6.4 · G15 G33a G33b
  needs: P0.1.4
  > the level matrix and the **never mock the thing under test** rule — for a converter "the thing" is the **no-harm/isolation LAYER** (`fs_guard`/`isolation`/`outcome`), tested with a real temp FS + a real isolated subprocess, NOT every engine in every L2 test (engine-INTERNAL behaviour is tested at L4 with real engines, exercised via fast corpus fixtures at L2). The a11y split: the §6.4.6a jsdom/`vitest-axe` ARIA leg (G33a) vs the Lane-B `@axe-core/webdriverio` contrast leg (G33b).
  > **Delivered (P0.5.1 — doctrine reconcile) [Build-Session-Entscheidung: P0.5.1]:** the test-levels matrix + the never-mock-the-thing-under-test rule (the "thing" = the no-harm/isolation LAYER `fs_guard`/`isolation`/`outcome`, real temp FS + real subprocess; engine-internals at the per-pair L4) + the a11y split (G33a `vitest-axe` ARIA / G33b `@axe-core/webdriverio` contrast) are authored in [`test-strategy.md`](../process/test-strategy.md) §0.1 + §1 + §1.7 (P0.1.4, the higher-ranked process doc per SSOT > spec > process > plan). No new artifact/gate-id; G15/G33a/G33b run when the React/Rust tests land (P1+).
- [x] **P0.5.2** [DOC] Author the property-test + flaky-test + no-stub conventions · §6.4.2 · G8 G16 G48
  needs: P0.1.4
  > **language-split:** Rust = `proptest` (macro-based shrinking, no manual `Shrink` impls); TS = `fast-check` (custom `Arbitrary` delegates to built-in shrinkers — ban `fc.gen()` without a shrink wrapper, machine-enforced by G9 invariant (f), P0.3.10). Determinism: pinned CI seed, a case-count floor above the thin default 256, a property failure NEVER retried to pass. Flaky-test policy: retry infra/timeout only, E2E-only auto-retry, determinism engineered (pinned locale/timezone, animations off). The "build fully, no skeleton/stub" rule wired to the deferral gate (G8).
  > **Delivered (P0.5.2 — doctrine reconcile) [Build-Session-Entscheidung: P0.5.2]:** the property-test language-split (Rust `proptest` / TS `fast-check`, the `fc.gen()`-shrink ban paired with G9 invariant (f)), determinism (pinned CI seed, case-count floor > 256, property-never-retried), the flaky-test policy (retry infra/timeout only, E2E-only auto-retry, engineered determinism), and the no-skeleton/stub rule wired to G8 are authored in [`test-strategy.md`](../process/test-strategy.md) §1.3 + §7 + §4 (P0.1.4). - [x] **P0.5.4** [GATE] Build the corpus / crash-fixture integrity gate + the LFS-resolution governance · §6.4.2 · G24a G24
  needs: P0.5.3
  > a committed **SHA-256 manifest of every tracked corpus/crash fixture** (+ the LFS-resolved `corpus-large` objects) verified in CI **before** the corpus runs, plus `git lfs fsck` on the Lane-B leg — these untrusted files are fed to the highest-privilege C/C++ decoders, so a poisoned/swapped fixture or redirected LFS pointer must surface as a manifest diff (a dual-review item), mirroring the `engines.lock` SHA discipline. G24a asserts every manifest path is `filter=lfs`-tracked per the EFFECTIVE `git check-attr filter` and `.lfsconfig` (if present) names only the canonical GitHub LFS endpoint; `.gitattributes` + `.lfsconfig` join the L(-1) security-critical-file set. **Manifest update protocol:** regenerated by the same `stage-corpus` step that adds a fixture (the generator built in **P0.5.11**), in the SAME commit; G24a fails on a stale manifest (`git diff --exit-code`); a plan-lint sub-check asserts every `fuzz/corpus/`+`corpus-large/` path has a manifest entry.
  > → activated in P1 (the manifest fills as corpus lands in P3–P7; the gate + protocol authored now). **Includes the auditable-provenance + manifested + ship-integrity legs (r15):** every corpus file carries a non-empty `provenance` source (URL / generator-ref / `self-produced`) + is manifested, and the corpus stays repo/CI-only (never in the installed app bundle — a `tests/corpus/` path in the staged bundle is caught by the G35 test-asset-exclusion sub-check); byte-level licence inference is not machine-decidable, so the gate enforces the auditable record, not a content-licence claim.

[`g24-corpus-integrity.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-corpus-integrity.py) = **44 legs** (freeze-gut ×4; row fields/licence ×5; sha bytes-vs-LFS-pointer-oid ×3; verify match/poison/dangling/LFS-tier ×4; lfs-tracking tracked/un-tracked/git-unavailable ×3; .lfsconfig absent/canonical/repointed/**pushurl/remote.lfsurl/lfspushurl/named-section/git-remote-not-flagged/quoted/comment/same-line/[include]/[includeIf]/direct-pin** ; bijection clean/un-manifested/git-unavailable/**subdir-manifest.toml/root-excluded/raw-unicode**; e2e target-absent/clean/poisoned/real-repo/**real-git-unicode-escape**); canary 34→35. Wired **L1** + **L2** + **L4** (`gate-tooling`, 3-OS). `check-corpus-integrity` is `scripts/check-*`-caged; `.gitattributes`+`.lfsconfig` are already L(-1)-caged (`l-neg1-files.toml`) — **no new cage entry, no new gate-id, no doc-fingerprints re-bless**. The `stage-corpus` generator the update-protocol invokes is the separate box **P0.5.11**. **G1 dual review (volle Härte, 2 Agent lenses + synthesis) NOGO → fixed → re-reviewed → fixed → GO:** both lenses found convergent **P1 fail-OPENs** — (1) the bijection skipped a non-ASCII fixture name (`git ls-files` C-quotes it; un-manifested untrusted byte escapes) → fixed `git -c core.quotePath=false ls-files -z` + NUL-split; (2) a subdir `manifest.toml` escaped the basename exclusion → fixed to an exact corpus-root-relative-path exclusion; (3) the `.lfsconfig` parser missed `lfs.pushurl`/`remote.*.lfsurl` (FETCH-tampering)/`remote.*.lfspushurl` → fixed a section-aware `parse_lfsconfig_endpoints` covering all 4 keys (quote/comment-aware, git-remote `url` correctly NOT flagged). The focused re-review then found a **further P1** — a `.lfsconfig` `[include]`/`includeIf` (git-lfs honours it, possibly into an un-committed file outside the reviewed tree, defeating the owner-ack) → fixed: any `[include]`/`[includeIf]` hard-fails (the endpoint must be a statically-verifiable direct pin). All four P1s verified empirically against the reviewers' exact attack variants; the 15 added legs are non-tautological (incl. a real-git e2e committing a unicode-named fixture). The §6.4.5 manifest example's omitted `sha256` field is **P0.5.11**'s concern (it generates the sha256 into the `[[file]]` rows).

- [x] **P0.5.11** [TEST] Build the `stage-corpus` SHA-256-manifest generator the P0.5.4 update protocol invokes · §6.4.5 §6.4.2 · G24a G24
  needs: P0.5.4
  > the tool the P0.5.4 manifest-update protocol ("regenerated by the same `stage-corpus` step that adds a fixture, in the SAME commit") + **every corpus-landing box (the primary per-format stagers AND the secondary edge/content-floor stagers — the authoritative set is each phase's own `needs: P0.5.11` edge, not this list, so the enumeration is never a closed-but-incomplete set: it spans P3.61; the image P5.48; the audio P6.30/P6.31; the video P6.57/P6.58; the to-GIF/extract-audio covers P6.75; the document P7.49/P7.50; the spreadsheet P7.61; the presentation P7.68; and the P9.31 adversarial-network corpus)** invoke but no box otherwise AUTHORS: a `scripts/stage-corpus` step that, given a new/changed `fuzz/corpus/`+`corpus-large/`+`tests/corpus/` fixture, (re)computes its SHA-256 and writes/updates the canonical row in the committed SHA-256 manifest deterministically (stable ordering, LF newlines) so the author never hand-computes a hash — making G24a's fail-closed `git diff --exit-code` staleness check a one-step regenerate, not an error-prone manual sync. **Plus a corpus-licence field-validation leg (G24a sub-check):** since fixtures ship in the public repo + LFS, the tool ASSERTS every `[[file]]` row carries a non-empty `licence` drawn from an allow-listed **redistributable** set (CC0/public-domain/self-produced/synthetic), turning the "each redistributable" prose every corpus-staging box asserts into a fail-closed manifest assertion — mirroring the `engines.lock` SPDX licence discipline (G36). Ships a **G24 positive+negative self-test** (a fixture added WITHOUT running `stage-corpus` leaves a stale manifest → G24a MUST fail; a `[[file]]` row with a missing/non-redistributable `licence` MUST fail; running the tool MUST produce a clean diff). Reuses the §6.4.5 manifest schema (`[[file]]` rows) the P4.60 bijection guard + the P0.5.4 LFS-resolution govern; tooling only — it generates + field-validates the manifest, it does not redefine the schema.
  > → activated immediately (the tool is buildable now over the empty/initial manifest; the corpus-landing boxes in P3/P5–P7 `needs:` it so the loop builds it first under DECISION C as the first corpus fixture lands).
  > **Delivered (P0.5.11):** [`scripts/stage-corpus`](../../scripts/stage-corpus) (stdlib, `tomllib`+`hashlib`). **REGENERATE (default):** for every `[[file]]` row in `tests/corpus/manifest.toml`, (re)computes the fixture's SHA-256 — an unresolved git-LFS pointer hashed via its `oid sha256:` (so it is correct pre-/post-`git lfs pull`, shared with G24a) — and writes it back into the row's `sha256` field; **`--check`** is the CI/pre-commit staleness+field assertion (no write). **FIELD-VALIDATION (the G24a sub-check):** every row must carry a non-empty `provenance` + a non-empty `licence` from the redistributable allow-list (`public-domain`/`CC0`/`self-produced`/`synthetic`) — a missing-file / non-redistributable-licence / empty-provenance row fails (exit 1). **[Build-Session-Entscheidung: P0.5.11]** the sha256 is written by a **SURGICAL per-`[[file]]`-block edit** (replace/insert the `sha256 = "…"` direct-key line), NOT a full canonical re-serialize — so the §6.4.5 schema is preserved EXACTLY (the `source`/`exercises`/`covers` arrays, the `[file.expect]` sub-table with its `"SOURCE→TARGET"` arrow-keys, the author's comments + row order), and the edit is **idempotent** (a re-run over an up-to-date manifest is byte-identical → a clean `git diff`, satisfying "deterministic, LF, the one-step regenerate"); orphan detection (an un-manifested committed corpus byte) is G24a's bijection (P0.5.4), not this writer. **Scope:** stage-corpus operates on the §6.4.5 ONE-root `tests/corpus/manifest.toml` (the same scope as G24a per the P0.5.4 decision (ii)); the requirement's `fuzz/corpus/`+`corpus-large/` surface is governed via that single manifest (the corpus-large LFS-tier rows resolve under it) + the **P0.5.8** fuzz box (the `fuzz/corpus/`+`fuzz/crashes/` set). A `[[file]]` header form the block-splitter cannot match (a quoted key) is **fail-closed** by a block-count-vs-`tomllib` cross-check (it refuses to edit a manifest it cannot fully split, never a false "clean"). Reuses the §6.4.5 `[[file]]` schema; does not redefine it. [`g24-stage-corpus.py`](../../scripts/gate-selftests/g24-stage-corpus.py) = **25 legs** (content_sha256 bytes/LFS-oid/malformed ×3; set_block_sha256 insert-after-path-before-`[file.expect]` / replace / **+ replace-after-a-multi-line-`covers`-array (no duplicate key)** ×3; split-block keeps the sub-table; **+ the G1-hardening legs: a trailing-comment `[[file]] # x` header is recognized + staged, a quoted-key `[["file"]]` header the splitter misses is fail-closed by the block-count-vs-`tomllib` cross-check**; regenerate: clean-validates / correct-sha / `[file.expect]`+`covers`+comment PRESERVED / idempotent ×5; e2e: stage-writes / `--check`-up-to-date / `--check`-stale-caught / re-stage-fixes / non-redistributable-licence-fails / empty-provenance-fails / missing-file-fails / target-absent / real-repo ×9); canary 35→36. **L(-1)-caged:** `scripts/stage-corpus` added to [`l-neg1-files.toml`](../../scripts/l-neg1-files.toml) (a poisoned generator could auto-vouch a swapped fixture whose sha would then "match" G24a) — the `l-neg1-cage` fingerprint re-blessed (`e5e4cbde…`→`2c6aae7c…`, computed via plan-lint's `_lf`) + the security-concept §2 enumeration and the build-gates G71 row prose synced in the same commit (CLAUDE.md §5 is explicitly non-exhaustive — no edit). The reassembly preamble-newline bug (a lost `\n` collapsed the blocks → always-"up-to-date") was caught + fixed BEFORE the G1 review (exact line-list reconstruction). NOT wired as an L1/L2/L4 gate (it is a dev TOOL the corpus-landing boxes invoke; G24a is the per-push verifier) — its g24 runs in the canary. **G1 dual review (volle Härte, ultracode Workflow: 2 lenses + opus synthesis) NOGO → fixed → re-reviewed GO:** the adversarial-skeptic lens found a real **P1** (correctness lens GO; STRICTER-WINS) — a `[[file]]` header with a TRAILING COMMENT (`[[file]] # x`, valid TOML) was not matched by the bare-header regex → the row collapsed into the preamble → no sha256 written, `--check` reported "clean" even after a fixture byte-swap, licence/provenance skipped → a STALE fixture escaped (P1 not P0 only because G24a fail-closes on the missing sha256). Fixed: `_FILE_HEADER_RE` accepts a trailing comment **+** a fail-closed block-count-vs-`tomllib` cross-check catches ANY other header form the splitter misses (a quoted key `[["file"]]`). The focused re-review returned **GO** (the critical `covers = [["A","B"]]` double-bracket false-positive case verified safe — regex + tomllib agree) and surfaced one **P3** (pre-existing, unreachable via the tool's own canonical output, fail-closed-detectable): `_direct_key_end` mistook a multi-line `covers` array's `["A","B"],` continuation for a sub-table start → a `sha256` placed after it could be duplicated; **fixed under ultracode** (the sub-table-header regex now requires `[`+identifier, not an array item). All verified empirically (incl. the §6.4.5 example with multi-line `covers` + `[file.expect]` round-tripping idempotently). The reassembly preamble-newline bug was caught + fixed BEFORE the review.

**Home:** docs/process/test-strategy.md · 06-build-test-release (§6.4 corpus/reliability; record the bomb fixtures §6.4.5 + the §2.14.1 mode-bit pin in the spec per the living-doc rule).
